External Services\n   140→\n   141→| Service | Protocol | Connected From | Purpose |\n   142→|---|---|---|---|\n   143→| Roboflow API | HTTPS | Backend (sync_worker), Backend (inference fallback) | Dataset sync, auto-labeling, cloud inference fallback |\n   144→| Firebase FCM | HTTPS | Worker (notification_worker), Mobile App | Push notifications to mobile devices |\n   145→| Twilio API | HTTPS | Error tracking |\n   150→\n   151→### 1.5 Pilot Additions (Session 20+)\n   152→\n   153→**Organizations Service** — New first-class entity for multi-tenancy. Organizations own stores, cameras, users, and edge agents. Plan-based limits (max_stores, max_cameras, max_edge_agents) enforced on creation.\n   154→\n   155→**Security Headers Middleware** — X-Frame-Options, HSTS, CSP, nosniff on all responses. Applied after RateLimiter, before CORS.\n   156→\n   157→**Prometheus /metrics** — FastAPI instrumentator exposing request metrics (latency histograms, request counts, in-progress gauges) at `/metrics` endpoint.\n   158→\n   159→**Dead Letter Queue** — Redis-backed DLQ for permanently failed Celery tasks. Tasks exceeding max retries are captured by `DeadLetterTask.on_failure` and pushed to a Redis list. Admin endpoints for viewing and replaying.\n   160→\n   161→**Backup Worker** — Daily mongodump to S3 via Celery Beat (3 AM UTC). Produces tar.gz archive uploaded to `backups/` S3 prefix with 30-day retention.\n   162→\n   163→---\n   164→\n   165→## 2. DATA FLOW SUMMARY\n   381→\n   382→### Detection Flow (Edge-First)\n   383→```\n   384→Camera --RTSP--> Edge Agent --HTTP--> Inference Server (ONNX)\n   385→                     |\n   386→                     v\n   387→              4-Layer Validation (local)\n   388→                     |\n   389→                     v\n   390→              Redis Buffer (offline queue)\n   391→                     |\n   392→                     v\n   393→              Uploader --HTTPS--> Cloud Backend --TCP--> MongoDB\n   394→                                       |\n   395→                                       v\n   396→                                  Redis PubSub --WS--> Web/Mobile clients\n   397→                                       |\n   398→                                       v\n   399→                                  Celery Worker --> Notifications\n   400→                                       |\n   401→                                  SMTP / FCM / Twilio / Webhook\n   402→```\n   403→\n   404→### Command Flow (Cloud to Edge)\n   405→```\n   406→Web UI --> Backend API --> MongoDB (edge_commands)\n   407→                              |\n   408→Edge Agent (polls /30s) <-----+\n   409→     |\n   410→     v\n   411→Execute: deploy_model, reload_config, restart_camera, etc.\n   412→```\n   413→\n   414→## 4. PORT MAP\n   415→\n   416→| Service | Port | Protocol | Binding |\n   417→|---|---|---|---|\n   418→| FastAPI Backend | 8000 | HTTP/WS | 0.0.0.0 |\n   419→| MongoDB | 27017 | TCP (Wire) | 0.0.0.0 (dev), internal (prod) |\n   420→| Redis (Cloud) | 6379 | TCP (RESP) | 0.0.0.0 (dev), internal (prod) |\n   421→| MinIO API | 9000 | HTTP (S3) | internal |\n   422→| MinIO Console | 9001 | HTTP | internal |\n   423→| Nginx | 80 | HTTP | 0.0.0.0 |\n   424→| Edge Inference Server | 8080 | HTTP | 127.0.0.1 only |\n   425→| Edge Agent Web UI | 8090 | HTTP | 0.0.0.0 |\n   426→| Edge Agent Config API | 8091 | HTTP | 0.0.0.0 |\n   427→| Edge Redis Buffer | 6379 | TCP (RESP) | internal |\n   428→| Web Dev Server (Vite) | 5173 | HTTP | dev only |\n   429→\n   430→## 5. KEY ARCHITECTURAL DECISIONS\n   431→\n   432→1. **Edge-first inference**: YOLO26 ONNX runs locally on edge GPU; cloud Roboflow is fallback only.\n   433→2. **Redis triple-duty**: Cache/PubSub (DB0), Celery broker (DB1), Celery results (DB2) -- single Redis instance in cloud.\n   434→3. **Separate edge Redis**: Independent Redis on edge for frame buffering with LRU eviction, survives cloud disconnection.\n   435→4. **Cloudflare Tunnel both sides**: Cloud side tunnels public traffic in; edge side tunnels to Cloudflare for secure egress without open ports.\n   436→5. **Polling not push for commands**: Edge agent polls backend every 30s for commands (no inbound ports needed).\n   437→6. **Circuit breaker pattern**: All notification channels (SMTP, FCM, Twilio, webhook) have independent circuit breakers.\n   438→7. **WebSocket via Redis PubSub**: Broadcasts work across multiple Gunicorn workers via PSUBSCRIBE on `ws:*` pattern.\n   439→\n   440→## 6. MONITORING STACK (Optional)\n   441→\n   442→| Component | Purpose | Port | Notes |\n   443→|---|---|---|---|\n   444→| **Prometheus** | Metrics collection + alerting | 9090 | Scrapes FastAPI `/metrics`, MongoDB exporter, Redis exporter |\n   445→| **Grafana** | Dashboards + visualization | 3000 | Pre-built dashboards for request latency, detection throughput, edge health |\n   446→| **MongoDB Exporter** | MongoDB metrics for Prometheus | 9216 | Exports replica set status, oplog, collection stats |\n   447→| **Redis Exporter** | Redis metrics for Prometheus | 9121 | Exports memory, keyspace, connected clients, command stats |\n   448→\n   449→Deployment: Optional `docker-compose.monitoring.yml` overlay. Edge (config_receiver.py `/api/alerts`) | REST + WebSocket alerts served to mobile on local WiFi |\n    58→\n    59→---\n    60→\n    61→## DETAILED DATA FLOWS\n    62→\n    63→### FLOW 1: Detection Flow (Camera Frame to Confirmed Detection)\n    64→\n    65→```\n    66→E1 (IP Camera)\n    67→  --[RTSP/HTTP stream]--> P1 (Frame Capture: ThreadedCameraCapture)\n    68→    --[base64 JPEG frame]--> P2 (ONNX Inference Server via HTTP localhost:8090)\n    69→      Steps inside P2:\n    70→        1. decode_image(base64) -> PIL Image\n    71→        2. apply_roi_mask(img, roi_polygon) -> masked image (blacks out outside ROI)\n    72→        3. preprocess(img) -> [1,3,640,640] float32 tensor\n    73→        4. session.run(None, {input: tensor}) -> raw output\n    74→        5. postprocess (auto-detect model type):\n    75→           - YOLOv8: [1,84,8400] -> NMS -> list[{class_id, confidence, bbox}]\n    76→           - YOLO26/NMS-free: [1,300,6] -> filter by confidence -> {"parentUuid":"dd802f85-389a-4c9c-86f2-5f6f9149c00b","isSidechain":true,"agentId":"a61ab2195b54edfce","message":{"model":"claude-opus-4-6","id":"msg_01XmJtTJh9bYTd4Azx6ujQmu","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"text","text":"I now have a thorough picture. Here is the complete re-audit report.\n\n---\n\n# FloorEye v2.0 Post-Fix Re-Audit Report\n\n**Date:** 2026-03-22\n**Scope:** 15 pilot fixes applied; re-audit of architecture, backend, and DevOps posture\n**Files Reviewed:** ARCHITECTURE.md, DATA_FLOW.md, ER_DIAGRAM.md, main.py, config.py, docker-compose.prod.yml, indexes.py, security_headers.py, rate_limiter.py, celery_app.py, dead_letter.py, backup_worker.py\n\n---\n\n## REVIEWER 1: SYSTEM ARCHITECT\n\n### What Was Fixed and Is Now Good\n\n1. **Security Gate (config.py lines 160-180)** -- Production startup blocks on insecure defaults for SECRET_KEY, EDGE_SECRET_KEY, ENCRYPTION_KEY, S3 credentials, and embedded Redis/Mongo passwords. This is well-implemented with a clear allowlist of known insecure defaults. **GOOD.**\n\n2. **Organizations Entity** -- First-class `organizations` collection with indexes on `id` (unique), `slug` (unique), and `is_active`. The ER diagram correctly shows org_id as a foreign key in users, stores, cameras, edge_agents, etc. Multi-tenancy hierarchy is now explicit. **GOOD.**\n\n3. **TTL Indexes** -- detection_logs (90d), system_logs (30d), audit_logs (365d), token_blacklist (dynamic on `expires_at`), password_reset_tokens (dynamic on `expires_at`). All implemented correctly with `expireAfterSeconds`. **GOOD.**\n\n4. **Idempotency Key** -- Sparse unique index on `detection_logs.idempotency_key` prevents duplicate frame uploads from edge agents. **GOOD.**\n\n5. **Architecture and Data Flow Diagrams** -- ARCHITECTURE.md is comprehensive: 449 lines, full component inventory, port map, ASCII diagram, correct Redis DB separation (DB0/DB1/DB2). DATA_FLOW.md covers all 7+ major flows with protocol details. ER_DIAGRAM.md has all 24 collections. These are production-quality reference docs. **GOOD.**\n\n### Remaining Issues\n\n**SA-01 | Middleware Ordering Is Inverted | Medium**\n- **Description:** FastAPI processes middleware in reverse add order (last added = outermost). In `main.py`, the add order is: RateLimitMiddleware (line 75), CORSMiddleware (line 78), SecurityHeadersMiddleware (line 87), TrustedHostMiddleware (line 91), Prometheus (line 98). This means the actual execution order is: Prometheus -> TrustedHost -> SecurityHeaders -> CORS -> RateLimiter -> handler. The ARCHITECTURE.md says \"RateLimiter -> SecurityHeaders -> CORS -> TrustedHost -> Prometheus\" but the actual execution is the opposite. Rate limiting happens *after* CORS and security headers, meaning a blocked 429 response still gets security headers (acceptable), but rate-limited requests still consume CORS processing.\n- **Impact:** Minor performance waste on rate-limited requests; the documented order misleads developers. Not a security vulnerability.\n- **Solution:** If the intent is to rate-limit before any other processing, move `RateLimitMiddleware` to be the last `add_middleware` call. Update ARCHITECTURE.md to match actual execution order.\n\n**SA-02 | No Content-Security-Policy Header | Medium**\n- **Description:** ARCHITECTURE.md section 1.5 mentions \"CSP\" as part of the SecurityHeadersMiddleware, but the actual `security_headers.py` does not set a `Content-Security-Policy` header. Only X-Frame-Options, nosniff, X-XSS-Protection, Referrer-Policy, Permissions-Policy, and HSTS (in production) are set.\n- **Impact:** Missing CSP allows potential XSS via inline script injection. X-XSS-Protection is deprecated in modern browsers and is not a substitute.\n- **Solution:** Add a restrictive CSP header: `default-src 'self'; script-src 'self'; style-src 'self' 'unsafe-inline'; img-src 'self' data: blob:; connect-src 'self' wss:;`. The `'unsafe-inline'` for styles is needed for Tailwind.\n\n**SA-03 | No `review_decisions` Collection Implementation | Low**\n- **Description:** The ER_DIAGRAM.md itself notes that `review_decisions` is defined in schemas.md but has no implementation code. There are no indexes, no service, no router for it.\n- **Impact:** If review queue decisions need to be persisted (for audit compliance, ML feedback loops), this is a gap. For pilot this is acceptable.\n- **Solution:** Implement `review_decisions` collection with service/router, or explicitly remove from schemas.md if not needed.\n\n**SA-04 | PATCH Method Not Allowed in CORS | Low**\n- **Description:** `main.py` line 82 only allows `[\"GET\", \"POST\", \"PUT\", \"DELETE\", \"OPTIONS\"]`. If any router uses PATCH (common for partial updates), it will be blocked by CORS for browser clients.\n- **Impact:** Low for now if no endpoints use PATCH, but limits future API design options.\n- **Solution:** Add `\"PATCH\"` to `allow_methods`.\n\n---\n\n## REVIEWER 2: BACKEND ENGINEER\n\n### What Was Fixed and Is Now Good\n\n1. **Rate Limiter (rate_limiter.py)** -- Redis-backed sliding window with in-memory fallback. Path normalization handles UUIDs and ObjectIds. Per-endpoint limits for auth/login (10/min), forgot/reset (5/min), detection (60/min). Default 1000/min. Pipeline-based atomic operations. **GOOD.**\n\n2. **Dead Letter Queue (dead_letter.py)** -- Captures permanently failed Celery tasks with task_id, name, args, kwargs, exception, and truncated traceback (2000 chars). Redis list with LTRIM to 1000 max items. Replay function pops from tail and re-queues. **GOOD.**\n\n3. **Backup Worker (backup_worker.py)** -- Celery Beat scheduled daily at 03:00 UTC. Uses `mongodump` with URI, compresses to tar.gz, uploads to S3 `backups/` prefix. Proper error handling for missing `mongodump` binary. **GOOD.**\n\n4. **Password Reset Tokens** -- Dedicated `password_reset_tokens` collection with unique index on `token`, `user_id` index, and TTL on `expires_at`. **GOOD.**\n\n5. **Idempotency on Detection Uploads** -- Sparse unique index on `idempotency_key` in detection_logs prevents duplicate processing from edge retry storms. **GOOD.**\n\n6. **Celery Configuration (celery_app.py)** -- `task_acks_late=True` with `worker_prefetch_multiplier=1` ensures tasks are not lost on worker crash. Dedicated queue routing for detection and notification tasks. JSON-only serialization prevents pickle deserialization attacks. **GOOD.**\n\n### Remaining Issues\n\n**BE-01 | Rate Limiter Checks After Adding Request | High**\n- **Description:** In the Redis path (lines 78-84), the pipeline executes: (1) remove old entries, (2) count current entries, (3) add new entry, (4) set expire. The count at step 2 is checked *before* the new entry is added (step 3), but all four commands are in a pipeline and execute atomically. The check `if count >= limit` on line 87 uses the count from *before* the add. This means the actual allowed requests per window is `limit + 1` because the request that pushes count to exactly `limit` passes the check, and its entry is already added.\n- **Impact:** Off-by-one: allows 11 login attempts instead of 10 per minute. Not critical but weakens brute-force protection.\n- **Solution:** Check `count + 1 >= limit` or swap the order: add first, then count, then conditionally remove if over limit.\n\n**BE-02 | In-Memory Fallback Not Cleaned Up | Medium**\n- **Description:** The in-memory `_fallback_counters` dict (line 55) grows without bound. Old keys are never evicted. If Redis is persistently down, this dict accumulates entries for every unique `(IP, method, path)` combination indefinitely.\n- **Impact:** Memory leak in the FastAPI process. Under sustained load with Redis down, could cause OOM.\n- **Solution:** Add periodic cleanup of stale keys, or use an LRU cache (e.g., `cachetools.TTLCache`) with a max size.\n\n**BE-03 | Backup Worker Uses Synchronous `boto3` in Celery Task | Medium**\n- **Description:** `backup_worker.py` uses synchronous `boto3.client` and `subprocess.run`, both of which block the Celery worker thread. This is actually acceptable for Celery (which runs synchronous code), but the bigger issue is that `mongodump` binary must be installed in the worker Docker image.\n- **Impact:** If the worker Dockerfile does not include `mongodb-database-tools`, the backup task will always fail silently (caught exception, logged, then raised). The `max_retries=1` means it retries once then goes to DLQ (if tasks use DeadLetterTask base), but the `run_backup` task does not inherit from `DeadLetterTask`.\n- **Solution:** (a) Ensure worker Dockerfile installs `mongodb-database-tools`. (b) Change task declaration to `base=DeadLetterTask` so permanent failures are captured. (c) Add a health check task that verifies `mongodump` exists on startup.\n\n**BE-04 | DeadLetterTask Not Used by Any Worker Task | High**\n- **Description:** `DeadLetterTask` is defined in `dead_letter.py` but the Celery tasks in `backup_worker.py`, `celery_app.py` beat schedule, and (likely) other workers use the default `@celery_app.task` decorator without `base=DeadLetterTask`. The DLQ infrastructure exists but is not wired up.\n- **Impact:** Failed tasks are lost to Celery's default failure handling. The DLQ will always be empty, giving a false sense of reliability.\n- **Solution:** Update all critical task decorators to include `base=DeadLetterTask`: notification workers, sync workers, backup worker, OTA worker.\n\n**BE-05 | Health Check Uses Synchronous Redis Client | Low**\n- **Description:** The `/api/v1/health` endpoint (main.py lines 113-120) creates a new synchronous `redis.from_url()` connection on every request, pings, and closes. In an async FastAPI application running under Gunicorn with Uvicorn workers, this blocks the event loop.\n- **Impact:** Health check latency spikes under load; could slow down other concurrent requests on the same worker.\n- **Solution:** Use `aioredis` or `redis.asyncio` for the health check, or cache the Redis client.\n\n**BE-06 | No `health_worker` in Celery Beat Schedule | Medium**\n- **Description:** `celery_app.py` beat_schedule only has `auto-close-stale-incidents` and `daily-backup`. The `health_worker.py` exists but is not scheduled. ARCHITECTURE.md mentions it should check MongoDB, Redis, and mark stale edge agents offline.\n- **Impact:** Stale edge agents are never automatically marked offline. The health monitoring described in docs does not actually run.\n- **Solution:** Add `health_worker.run_health_check` to beat_schedule with an appropriate interval (e.g., every 60 seconds).\n\n---\n\n## REVIEWER 3: DEVOPS\n\n### What Was Fixed and Is Now Good\n\n1. **MongoDB Auth in docker-compose.prod.yml** -- Uses `${MONGO_ROOT_USER}` and `${MONGO_ROOT_PASSWORD}` environment variables, not hardcoded credentials. Healthcheck uses `mongosh` ping. **GOOD.**\n\n2. **Redis Auth** -- Uses `--requirepass ${REDIS_PASS}` with healthcheck that passes the password. **GOOD.**\n\n3. **Prometheus Metrics** -- `prometheus-fastapi-instrumentator>=7.0.0` in requirements.txt, instrumented in main.py with `/health` and `/metrics` excluded from tracking. Exposed at `/metrics`. **GOOD.**\n\n4. **Service Health Checks and Dependencies** -- MongoDB, Redis, and MinIO all have health checks with interval/timeout/retries. Backend and worker depend on `service_healthy` condition for MongoDB and Redis. **GOOD.**\n\n5. **Security Headers** -- HSTS only in production, X-Frame-Options DENY, nosniff, Permissions-Policy restrictive. **GOOD.**\n\n### Remaining Issues\n\n**DO-01 | No Network Isolation in docker-compose.prod.yml | Critical**\n- **Description:** No Docker networks are defined. All services (backend, worker, mongodb, redis, minio, cloudflared, web) are on the default bridge network and can all reach each other on all ports. MongoDB (27017), Redis (6379), and MinIO (9000/9001) are accessible from every container.\n- **Impact:** If the web container (nginx) is compromised, attacker has direct TCP access to MongoDB and Redis. Violates principle of least privilege.\n- **Solution:** Define `frontend` and `backend` networks. Put web+cloudflared on `frontend`, backend+worker+mongodb+redis+minio on `backend`. Only backend gets both networks.\n\n**DO-02 | No Resource Limits on Any Service | High**\n- **Description:** No `deploy.resources.limits` (CPU/memory) on any service in docker-compose.prod.yml. A single runaway process (e.g., a detection worker loop, or a MongoDB query loading large result sets) can consume all host resources and crash everything.\n- **Impact:** No protection against noisy-neighbor or OOM scenarios. A backup task running mongodump could temporarily spike memory and starve the backend.\n- **Solution:** Add memory and CPU limits: backend (2GB/2CPU), worker (4GB/2CPU), mongodb (4GB/2CPU), redis (512MB/1CPU), minio (1GB/1CPU), web (256MB/0.5CPU).\n\n**DO-03 | No Log Driver Configuration | Medium**\n- **Description:** No logging configuration in docker-compose.prod.yml. All containers use the default `json-file` driver with no max-size or max-file limits.\n- **Impact:** Logs accumulate indefinitely on disk. Detection logs at high throughput can fill the disk within days/weeks, causing Docker to fail.\n- **Solution:** Add `logging: driver: json-file, options: max-size: \"50m\", max-file: \"5\"` to all services, or configure a centralized log driver (e.g., fluentd).\n\n**DO-04 | MinIO Port Exposure Not Controlled | Medium**\n- **Description:** MinIO has no `ports` mapping in docker-compose.prod.yml (good -- not exposed to host), but the console on 9001 is accessible from within the Docker network by any container. There is also no TLS between backend and MinIO.\n- **Impact:** Internal-only risk. If web container is compromised, attacker could access MinIO console. No data-in-transit encryption between backend and MinIO.\n- **Solution:** Add network isolation (see DO-01). For TLS, either use MinIO's built-in TLS or accept the risk for internal traffic with documented rationale.\n\n**DO-05 | Redis Not Configured for Persistence in Production | Medium**\n- **Description:** Redis is started with `redis-server --requirepass ${REDIS_PASS}` but no explicit persistence configuration (no `--appendonly yes`, no `--save` directives). The volume `redis_data:/data` is mounted, but Redis defaults may not persist data reliably.\n- **Impact:** Redis restart could lose rate limit state (acceptable), Celery broker messages (tasks in flight), and PubSub state. Celery tasks queued but not yet picked up would be lost.\n- **Solution:** Add `--appendonly yes --appendfsync everysec` to the Redis command for reliable task queue persistence.\n\n**DO-06 | Cloudflared Volume Uses `${USERPROFILE}` (Windows-Specific) | High**\n- **Description:** Line 88: `${USERPROFILE}/.cloudflared:/etc/cloudflared:ro` uses the Windows `%USERPROFILE%` env var. This will fail on Linux production servers where the variable is typically `$HOME`.\n- **Impact:** Cloudflared will fail to start on Linux deployments, breaking all public access through the tunnel.\n- **Solution:** Change to `${HOME}/.cloudflared:/etc/cloudflared:ro` or use a fixed path like `./cloudflared:/etc/cloudflared:ro`.\n\n**DO-07 | No Backup Retention/Cleanup | Medium**\n- **Description:** The backup_worker uploads to `backups/{timestamp}.tar.gz` but never deletes old backups. The ARCHITECTURE.md mentions \"30-day retention\" but no lifecycle policy or cleanup code exists.\n- **Impact:** S3/MinIO storage grows indefinitely. At scale, backup storage costs accumulate.\n- **Solution:** Add S3 lifecycle policy on the `backups/` prefix for 30-day expiration, or add a Celery task that deletes backups older than 30 days.\n\n**DO-08 | Worker Dockerfile May Lack `mongodump` | Medium**\n- **Description:** `backup_worker.py` depends on `mongodump` being available in the worker container. The worker uses `Dockerfile.worker` but it is unclear if `mongodb-database-tools` is installed.\n- **Impact:** Daily backup task will fail every run until the binary is installed.\n- **Solution:** Add `mongodb-database-tools` to the worker Dockerfile, or use `pymongo`'s streaming dump approach instead of shelling out.\n\n---\n\n## SUMMARY SCORECARD\n\n| Area | Fixed (Good) | Remaining Issues | Critical | High | Medium | Low |\n|------|-------------|-----------------|----------|------|--------|-----|\n| System Architecture | 5 | 4 | 0 | 0 | 2 | 2 |\n| Backend Engineering | 6 | 6 | 0 | 2 | 3 | 1 |\n| DevOps | 5 | 8 | 1 | 2 | 5 | 0 |\n| **TOTAL** | **16** | **18** | **1** | **4** | **10** | **3** |\n\n## PILOT DEPLOYMENT RISK ASSESSMENT\n\n**Overall Verdict: Conditionally Ready for Pilot -- with 5 mandatory fixes before go-live.**\n\nThe 15 fixes significantly improved the security and operational posture. The security gate, MongoDB auth, TTL indexes, rate limiter, and DLQ infrastructure are all solid additions. However:\n\n**Must-fix before pilot (blocks deployment):**\n1. **DO-01** (Network isolation) -- Single compromised container = full database access\n2. **DO-06** (USERPROFILE path) -- Cloudflared will not start on Linux production\n3. **BE-04** (DeadLetterTask not wired) -- DLQ exists but catches nothing\n4. **DO-02** (Resource limits) -- No OOM protection in production\n\n**Should-fix for pilot reliability:**\n5. **BE-06** (health_worker not scheduled) -- Stale edge agents never cleaned up\n6. **DO-05** (Redis persistence) -- Celery tasks lost on Redis restart\n7. **SA-02** (Missing CSP header) -- XSS protection gap\n8. **DO-03** (Log rotation) -- Disk fill risk within weeks"}],"stop_reason":"end_turn","stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":1,"cache_creation_input_tokens":415,"cache_read_input_tokens":47498,"output_tokens":4765,"server_tool_use":{"web_search_requests":0,"web_fetch_requests":0},"service_tier":"standard","cache_creation":{"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":415},"inference_geo":"","iterations":[],"speed":"standard"}},"requestId":"req_011CZKDUJ4ByjMHB7tcG2cwA","type":"assistant","uuid":"32509209-b8e3-40b5-a59a-817cb587c4a1","timestamp":"2026-03-23T02:24:38.393Z","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"C:\\Users\\jshah\\flooreye","sessionId":"31c38874-0fdd-46a7-87a9-fa414d8b993d","version":"2.1.81","gitBranch":"main","slug":"warm-exploring-rossum"}

db.edge_agents.find_one({\"id\": payload[\"sub\"]})\n    53→    if not agent:\n    54→        raise HTTPException(status_code=status.HTTP_401_UNAUTHORIZED, detail=\"Agent not found\")\n    55→ 851→organizations ─────1:N────→ stores        (org has many stores)\n   852→organizations ─────1:N────→ users         (org has many users)\n   853→organizations ─────1:N────→ cameras       (org has many cameras, via org_id)\n   854→organizations ─────1:N────→ edge_agents   (org has many agents)\n   855→\n   856→users ─────1:N────→ password_reset_tokens (user may have reset tokens)\n   857→users ─────1:N────→ user_devices          (user has many mobile devices)\n   858→users ─────1:N────→ audit_logs            (user generates many audit entries)\n   859→users ─────1:N────→ review_decisions      (user reviews many detections)\n   860→users ─────1:N────→ token_blacklist       (user has many blacklisted tokens)\n   861→\n   862→stores ────1:N────→ cameras               (store has many cameras)\n   863→stores ────1:N────→ edge_agents           (store has many edge agents)\n   864→stores ────1:N────→ devices               (store has many IoT devices)\n   865→stores ────1:N────→ events                (store has many incidents)\n   866→stores ────1:N────→ detection_logs        (store has many detections)\n   867→stores ────1:N────→ clips                 (store has many clips)\n   868→stores ────1:N────→ dataset_frames        (store may have many dataset frames)\n   869→\n   870→cameras ───1:N────→ rois                  (camera has many ROI versions)\n   871→cameras ───1:N────→ dry_references        (camera has many dry ref versions)\n   872→cameras ───1:N────→ detection_logs        (camera generates many detections)\n   873→cameras ───1:N────→ events                (camera generates many incidents)\n   874→cameras ───1:N────→ clips                 (camera has many clips)\n   875→cameras ───1:N────→ dataset_frames        (camera may source many frames)\n   876→cameras ───N:1────→ edge_agents           (camera optionally assigned to agent)\n   877→\n   878→edge_agents─1:N───→ edge_commands         (agent has many pending commands)\n   879→edge_agents─1:N───→ devices               (agent optionally controls devices)\n   880→\n   881→events ────1:N────→ detection_logs        (incident groups many detections)\n   882→events ────1:N────→ clips                 (incident may trigger many clips)\n   883→events ────1:N────→ notification_deliveries (incident triggers notifications)\n   884→\n   885→detection_logs─1:N→ review_decisions      (detection has many review decisions)\n   886→detection_logs─N:1→ events                (detection belongs to one incident)\n   887→\n   888→notification_rules─1:N→ notification_deliveries (rule generates deliveries)\n   889→notification_rules─N:1→ stores            (rule optionally scoped to store)\n   890→notification_rules─N:1→ cameras           (rule optionally scoped to camera)\n   891→\n   892→dataset_frames─1:1→ annotations           (frame has one annotation set)\n   893→annotations ──N:1──→ dataset_frames       (annotation references one frame)\n   894→\n   895→model_versions─N:1→ training_jobs         (model produced by one training job)\n   896→training_jobs ─1:1→ model_versions        (job produces one model, bidirectional)\n   897→\n   898→integration_configs → (standalone, org-scoped)\n   899→detection_control_settings → (scope polymorphic: references stores or cameras via scope_id)\n   900→detection_class_overrides  → Properly supports multi-tenancy.\n\n2. **Password reset tokens collection indexed** -- `indexes.py` lines 211-215: `token` (unique), `user_id`, TTL on `expires_at`. Correct.\n\n3. **Password reset implemented** -- `auth.py` lines 142-229: `forgot-password` and `reset-password` are no longer 501 stubs. Tokens are generated, stored with expiry, and validated before password change.\n\n4. **Insecure default detection** -- `config.py` lines 8-16, 160-180: Production startup blocked if `SECRET_KEY`, `EDGE_SECRET_KEY`, `ENCRYPTION_KEY`, `S3_ACCESS_KEY_ID`, `S3_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY`, `REDIS_URL`, or `MONGODB_URI` contain insecure defaults. This is thorough.\n\n5. **Security headers middleware** -- `security_headers.py`: `X-Content-Type-Options`, `X-Frame-Options`, `X-XSS-Protection`, `Referrer-Policy`, `Permissions-Policy`, and `Strict-Transport-Security` (production only). Solid baseline.\n\n6. **Store access RBAC** -- `org_filter.py` lines 13-36: `store_access_query()` correctly restricts non-admin roles to their assigned stores, returns impossible query (`$in: []`) for users with no store access.\n\n7. **Detection log TTL** -- `indexes.py` line 70: TTL on `timestamp` field using `DETECTION_LOG_RETENTION_DAYS * 86400` (configurable, default 90 days). Correct.\n\n8. **Idempotency on edge frame/detection uploads** -- `edge.py` lines 320-327, 389-397: MD5-based idempotency key computed from camera+confidence+area+inference_time, with sparse unique index in `indexes.py` line 73.\n\n9. **Dead letter queue** -- `dead_letter.py`: Redis-backed DLQ with capped size (1000), replay capability. Functional.\n\n10. **Backup worker** -- `backup_worker.py`: mongodump + tar.gz + S3 upload via Celery. Basic but functional.\n\n11. **Detection control cache invalidation** -- `detection_control_service.py` lines 139-160: Cache invalidation on upsert for camera, store, org, and global scopes. Falls back to 60s TTL on failure.\n\n12. **Audit log TTL** -- `indexes.py` lines 167-176: TTL on `created_at`, configurable via `AUDIT_LOG_RETENTION_DAYS` (default 365 days).\n\n13. **Test infrastructure** -- `conftest.py`: Proper async test DB isolation, per-test cleanup, dependency override, admin/viewer fixtures, org fixture.\n\n14. **Account lockout settings** -- `config.py` lines 121-122: `AUTH_MAX_FAILED_ATTEMPTS=5`, `AUTH_LOCKOUT_MINUTES=15`.\n\n15. **Edge incident dedup on sync** -- `edge.py` lines 632-653: Checks both `edge_incident_id` match AND time-window dedup against cloud-created incidents.\n\n---\n\n## REMAINING FINDINGS\n\n### ROLE 1: DATABASE ENGINEER\n\n**DB-001 | review_decisions collection has no indexes in indexes.py | Severity: MEDIUM**\n- **Description:** The ER diagram (line 766-767) explicitly notes \"no indexes.py entry; no service implementation found.\" The `review_decisions` schema is in `docs/schemas.md` but the collection is never indexed and has no service code.\n- **Impact:** If review queue functionality is used, queries on `(org_id, detection_id)` and `(reviewed_by)` will be full collection scans.\n- **Solution:** Either add indexes for `review_decisions` in `indexes.py`, or remove the schema definition if the feature was replaced by the flag/unflag workflow.\n\n**DB-002 | integration_test_history collection has no indexes | Severity: LOW**\n- **Description:** Per ER diagram line 837: \"IDX: none defined in indexes.py.\" This collection is written to by the integrations router/service.\n- **Impact:** Queries on `(org_id, service, tested_at)` will be unindexed scans. Low volume mitigates this for pilot.\n- **Solution:** Add compound index `(org_id, service, tested_at DESC)` in `indexes.py`.\n\n**DB-003 | training_jobs collection has no indexes in indexes.py | Severity: LOW**\n- **Description:** ER diagram lines 463-464 notes indexes are \"presumed.\" The collection exists in `schemas.md` and `models/training_job.py` but has no indexes created.\n- **Impact:** Training job queries by `(org_id, status)` will be unindexed. Low volume during pilot.\n- **Solution:** Add `(id) unique`, `(org_id, status)` indexes.\n\n**DB-004 | token_blacklist has no unique index on jti | Severity: MEDIUM**\n- **Description:** `indexes.py` line 198 creates `IndexModel([(\"jti\", ASCENDING)])` but NOT `unique=True`. The `logout_all` endpoint (auth.py line 113) inserts `jti: \"__all__\"` which could create duplicates if called multiple times.\n- **Impact:** Duplicate blacklist entries waste space. More critically, the non-unique index means a compromised token's JTI could theoretically be inserted twice without error, which is benign but indicates schema sloppiness.\n- **Solution:** Make `jti` index unique, or add compound unique on `(user_id, jti)`.\n\n**DB-005 | No cascade cleanup for store deletion | Severity: MEDIUM**\n- **Description:** ER diagram lines 920-930 confirm: \"deleting a store does not auto-delete its cameras.\" Orphaned cameras, detection_logs, events, clips, devices, and edge_agents would remain with invalid `store_id` references.\n- **Impact:** Data integrity issues post-deletion. Queries filtering by store_id return orphaned data.\n- **Solution:** Implement cascade delete or soft-delete-only pattern for stores (disallow hard delete).\n\n---\n\n### ROLE 2: SECURITY ENGINEER\n\n**SEC-001 | Password reset token uses uuid4 instead of cryptographic random | Severity: MEDIUM**\n- **Description:** `auth.py` line 157: `token = str(uuid.uuid4())`. UUIDv4 uses `os.urandom` internally in CPython so it is cryptographically random in practice, but the token is only 122 bits of entropy (36 hex chars with dashes). Industry best practice is `secrets.token_urlsafe(32)` for 256-bit tokens.\n- **Impact:** Acceptable entropy for pilot but below OWASP recommendation of 256-bit reset tokens.\n- **Solution:** Replace with `import secrets; token = secrets.token_urlsafe(32)`.\n\n**SEC-002 | Password reset does not invalidate existing sessions | Severity: HIGH**\n- **Description:** `auth.py` lines 216-227: After resetting password, the code updates `password_hash` and marks the token as used, but does NOT blacklist existing JWTs or call `logout_all`. A compromised session remains valid for up to `ACCESS_TOKEN_EXPIRE_MINUTES` (15 min) after password reset.\n- **Impact:** If password was reset because of account compromise, attacker retains access for up to 15 minutes.\n- **Solution:** After password reset, insert a `token_blacklist` entry with `jti: \"__all__\"` for the user, same as `logout_all` does.\n\n**SEC-003 | No rate limiting on forgot-password endpoint | Severity: MEDIUM**\n- **Description:** The `forgot-password` endpoint has no per-IP or per-email rate limit. An attacker could flood the token table and potentially cause email spam if SMTP is configured.\n- **Impact:** DDoS vector on email infrastructure; token table bloat (mitigated by TTL auto-cleanup).\n- **Solution:** Add rate limiting (e.g., 3 requests per email per hour, 10 per IP per hour).\n\n**SEC-004 | SMTP credentials passed in cleartext from integration config | Severity: MEDIUM**\n- **Description:** `auth.py` lines 177-188: SMTP password is retrieved from `config.get(\"password\", \"\")` and used directly. The integration_configs store encrypted values, but the `get_integration` function presumably decrypts. However, the SMTP connection uses `starttls()` -- if the SMTP server doesn't support TLS, credentials are sent in cleartext.\n- **Impact:** SMTP credentials could be intercepted on non-TLS connections.\n- **Solution:** Verify TLS is established before `server.login()`, or use `SMTP_SSL` as alternative.\n\n**SEC-005 | Security headers missing Content-Security-Policy | Severity: LOW**\n- **Description:** `security_headers.py` does not set `Content-Security-Policy`. While the API is primarily JSON, any HTML error pages or swagger docs could be vulnerable to XSS without CSP.\n- **Impact:** Low risk for API-only backend, but missing defense-in-depth.\n- **Solution:** Add basic CSP: `default-src 'self'`.\n\n**SEC-006 | MD5 used for idempotency key hashing | Severity: LOW**\n- **Description:** `edge.py` line 321: `hashlib.md5(idem_key.encode()).hexdigest()[:16]`. MD5 is not used for security here (collision resistance for idempotency), but it raises audit flags.\n- **Impact:** Theoretical collision risk with 16-char hex (64 bits). Not a security vulnerability but a code smell.\n- **Solution:** Use `hashlib.sha256` and take first 16 chars for consistency with security practices.\n\n---\n\n### ROLE 3: QA ENGINEER\n\n**Current test count: 54 tests across 11 test files.**\n\nThis is a significant improvement from the previously reported 24 tests. Test files:\n\n| File | Tests | Coverage Area |\n|------|-------|--------------|\n| test_auth.py | 7 | Login, me, users CRUD, RBAC |\n| test_stores.py | 6 | CRUD, auth, not-found |\n| test_cameras.py | 4 | List, filter, auth |\n| test_detection.py | 5 | History, flagging, events |\n| test_incidents.py | 6 | List, filters, auth, ack/resolve |\n| test_edge.py | 3 | List, provision |\n| test_integrations.py | 5 | List, save, get, delete |\n| test_detection_control.py | 4 | Get, upsert, effective, delete |\n| test_notifications.py | 4 | Rules, deliveries, auth |\n| test_mobile.py | 4 | Dashboard, alerts, analytics, auth |\n| test_organizations.py | 6 | CRUD, slug unique, auth |\n\n**QA-001 | No tests for password reset flow | Severity: HIGH**\n- **Description:** The newly implemented `forgot-password` and `reset-password` endpoints have zero test coverage.\n- **Impact:** A critical security-sensitive flow (password reset) is untested. Regressions could go undetected.\n- **Solution:** Add tests: happy path, expired token, used token, invalid token, non-existent email.\n\n**QA-002 | No tests for edge frame/detection upload with idempotency | Severity: HIGH**\n- **Description:** The edge `upload_frame` and `upload_detection` endpoints -- the highest-traffic endpoints in production -- have no tests. The idempotency dedup logic is untested.\n- **Impact:** The core data ingestion pipeline is untested. Any regression breaks the entire detection system.\n- **Solution:** Add tests: frame upload, detection upload, duplicate detection (idempotency), incident creation on wet detection.\n\n**QA-003 | No tests for edge incident sync | Severity: MEDIUM**\n- **Description:** The `sync_incidents_from_edge` endpoint (edge.py lines 599-755) is a complex 150-line function with dedup logic, merge logic, and notification dispatch -- all untested.\n- **Impact:** Edge autonomy feature has zero test coverage.\n- **Solution:** Add tests: new incident sync, duplicate sync, merge with cloud incident, notification dispatch.\n\n**QA-004 | No tests for DLQ or backup worker | Severity: LOW**\n- **Description:** `dead_letter.py` and `backup_worker.py` have no tests.\n- **Impact:** Infrastructure resilience code is untested.\n- **Solution:** Add unit tests with mocked Redis/S3 for DLQ push/pop/replay and backup flow.\n\n**QA-005 | No tests for detection control inheritance chain | Severity: MEDIUM**\n- **Description:** Only basic get/upsert/delete settings are tested. The inheritance resolution (global -> org -> store -> camera) and cache behavior are untested.\n- **Impact:** The 4-layer inheritance chain -- a core feature -- could silently break.\n- **Solution:** Add tests: multi-layer inheritance, cache hit/miss, cache invalidation on update.\n\n**QA-006 | No integration or load tests | Severity: MEDIUM**\n- **Description:** All tests are unit/endpoint-level. No end-to-end flow tests (e.g., edge detection -> incident creation -> notification dispatch), no load tests.\n- **Impact:** Cannot validate system behavior under realistic conditions.\n- **Solution:** Add at least one end-to-end smoke test and basic load test for the frame upload endpoint.\n\n**QA-007 | No tests for WebSocket functionality | Severity: MEDIUM**\n- **Description:** The WebSocket hub (publish_detection, publish_incident) is called from multiple endpoints but has zero test coverage.\n- **Impact:** Real-time dashboard updates could break without detection.\n- **Solution:** Add WebSocket connection tests using httpx-ws or similar.\n\n---\n\n### ROLE 4: RELIABILITY ENGINEER\n\n**REL-001 | Backup worker has no scheduling or monitoring | Severity: HIGH**\n- **Description:** `backup_worker.py` defines a Celery task but there is no Celery Beat schedule or cron job to trigger it. There is also no alerting if backups fail.\n- **Impact:** Backups never run unless manually triggered. Data loss risk for pilot.\n- **Solution:** Add Celery Beat schedule (e.g., daily at 02:00 UTC). Add Sentry/system_log alert on backup failure. Add a `/api/v1/admin/backup-status` endpoint.\n\n**REL-002 | DLQ has no monitoring or alerting | Severity: MEDIUM**\n- **Description:** `dead_letter.py` writes to Redis and logs a warning, but there is no periodic check, no dashboard, and no alert when DLQ depth exceeds a threshold.\n- **Impact:** Failed tasks silently accumulate. Operators have no visibility into system health.\n- **Solution:** Add a periodic health check that alerts when `DLQ_KEY` length exceeds a configurable threshold (e.g., 10).\n\n**REL-003 | Detection control settings cache has stale data window | Severity: LOW**\n- **Description:** `detection_control_service.py` line 241: Cache TTL is 60 seconds. Cache invalidation on upsert (lines 139-160) is best-effort (catches exceptions silently). If Redis is briefly unavailable during an update, stale settings persist for up to 60 seconds.\n- **Impact:** A camera could use outdated detection thresholds for up to 60 seconds after a settings change. Acceptable for pilot but should be documented.\n- **Solution:** Document the 60s staleness window. Consider reducing TTL to 30s for more responsive updates. Optionally add a \"purge cache\" admin endpoint.\n\n**REL-004 | Idempotency key collision risk | Severity: MEDIUM**\n- **Description:** `edge.py` line 321: The idempotency key is `md5(camera:confidence:area:inference_time)[:16]` -- only 64 bits. Two distinct detections with identical confidence, area, and inference_time from the same camera will collide and the second will be silently dropped.\n- **Impact:** Legitimate detections could be deduplicated incorrectly if they have identical numeric values. This is especially likely with rounded confidence values (e.g., 0.8500, 0.8500).\n- **Solution:** Include timestamp or a monotonic counter in the idempotency key. Alternatively, let the edge agent generate its own idempotency key (a UUID per detection) and pass it in the request body.\n\n**REL-005 | No health check endpoint for edge agents to verify connectivity | Severity: LOW**\n- **Description:** Edge agents use `/heartbeat` to report status, but there is no lightweight `/health` or `/ping` endpoint that does not require auth for basic connectivity testing.\n- **Impact:** Edge agents cannot distinguish between \"cloud is down\" and \"my token is invalid\" without parsing error responses.\n- **Solution:** Add a public `/api/v1/health` or `/api/v1/edge/ping` endpoint.\n\n**REL-006 | Single Redis instance is a single point of failure | Severity: HIGH**\n- **Description:** Redis is used for Celery broker, result backend, DLQ, detection control cache, and rate limiting. A single Redis instance failure takes down background processing, caching, and task queuing simultaneously.\n- **Impact:** Complete system degradation if Redis goes down. Detection uploads still work (direct MongoDB), but incident processing, notifications, and cache all fail.\n- **Solution:** For pilot: document as known risk, ensure Redis has persistence (AOF/RDB). For production: deploy Redis Sentinel or Redis Cluster.\n\n**REL-007 | Backup worker uses subprocess mongodump with no fallback | Severity: MEDIUM**\n- **Description:** `backup_worker.py` line 30: Relies on `mongodump` binary being installed. Line 34-36: If not found, raises `FileNotFoundError` with `max_retries=1`, meaning it retries once and fails permanently.\n- **Impact:** If the worker container does not have `mongodb-database-tools` installed, backups silently fail forever.\n- **Solution:** Ensure `mongodb-database-tools` is in the worker Dockerfile. Add a startup health check that verifies `mongodump` is available.\n\n**REL-008 | No graceful degradation for S3 upload failures | Severity: MEDIUM**\n- **Description:** `edge.py` lines 293-303, 307-317: S3 upload failures are silently caught (`except Exception: pass`). The detection is still saved to MongoDB but with `frame_s3_path: None`.\n- **Impact:** Frame images are permanently lost if S3 is down. No retry mechanism, no local fallback storage.\n- **Solution:** On S3 failure, queue a retry via Celery DLQ. Optionally store frame_base64 temporarily in the detection_log document for later upload.\n\n---\n\n## SUMMARY SCORECARD\n\n| Role | Resolved | Remaining | Critical/High | Medium | Low |\n|------|----------|-----------|---------------|--------|-----|\n| Database Engineer | 5 | 5 | 0 | 3 | 2 |\n| Security Engineer | 4 | 6 | 1 | 3 | 2 |\n| QA Engineer | 1 | 7 | 2 | 4 | 1 |\n| Reliability Engineer | 5 | 8 | 2 | 4 | 2 |\n| **TOTAL** | **15** | **26** | **5** | **14** | **7** |\n\n**Pilot readiness:** The 15 fixes meaningfully improved the codebase. The security gate, indexes, password reset, RBAC, and DLQ/backup infrastructure are all functional. However, 5 high-severity findings remain -- particularly around test coverage for critical paths (password reset, edge ingestion), backup scheduling, session invalidation after password reset, and Redis as a single point of failure.
